  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fefcbe7f-1dbe-4d3e-9e4a-b36f84aecb43'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11733716662050555027">The classic inspirational parable from the top motivation and marketing trainer and #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>The Millionaire Messenger</i>—a triumphant tale of personal growth and change that will inspire anyone who has ever wished for a second chance.<br/><br/>What if you were handed a golden ticket that could magically start your life anew?<br/><br/>That question is at the heart </span>
  <span id="freeText11733716662050555027" style="display:none">The classic inspirational parable from the top motivation and marketing trainer and #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>The Millionaire Messenger</i>—a triumphant tale of personal growth and change that will inspire anyone who has ever wished for a second chance.<br /><br />What if you were handed a golden ticket that could magically start your life anew?<br /><br />That question is at the heart of <i>Life’s Golden Ticket</i>. Brendon Burchard tells the story of a man who is so trapped in the prison of his past that he cannot see the possibilities, the choices, and the gifts before him. To soothe his fiancée Mary, clinging to life in a hospital bed, the man takes the envelope she offers and heads to an old, abandoned amusement park that she begs him to visit.<br /><br />To his surprise, when he steps through the rusted entrance gates, the park magically comes to life. Guided by the wise groundskeeper Henry, the man will encounter park employees, answer difficult questions, overcome obstacles, listen to lessons from those wiser than he, and take a hard look at himself.<br /><br />At the end of his journey, the man opens Mary’s mysterious envelope. Inside is a golden ticket—the final phase in turning his tragic life’s story of loss and regret into a triumphant tale of love and redemption.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11733716662050555027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_186238631" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186238631" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186238631?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186238631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6619538284042740239">Fun book<br/><br/>If you liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40874325.The_Shack' title='The Shack by William Paul Young' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shack</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3431.The_Five_People_You_Meet_in_Heaven' title='The Five People You Meet in Heaven by Mitch Albom' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Five People You Meet in Heaven</a>, you will probably like this. <br/><br/>The metaphors are not too subtle and the symbols a little too over the top, not one of the better in this genre (does this even have a specific genre?) but a good book nonetheless. Turns out Burchard is a motivational speaker and life coach so throw in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/865.The_Alchemist' title='The Alchemist by Paulo Coelho' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Alchemist</a> too. Maybe this is a genre: the fantasized and personified performance art as extended motivation / self help.<br/><br/>I do like the carnivales</span>
  <span id="freeText6619538284042740239" style="display:none">Fun book<br><br>If you liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40874325.The_Shack" title="The Shack by William Paul Young" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shack</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3431.The_Five_People_You_Meet_in_Heaven" title="The Five People You Meet in Heaven by Mitch Albom" rel="nofollow noopener">The Five People You Meet in Heaven</a>, you will probably like this. <br><br>The metaphors are not too subtle and the symbols a little too over the top, not one of the better in this genre (does this even have a specific genre?) but a good book nonetheless. Turns out Burchard is a motivational speaker and life coach so throw in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/865.The_Alchemist" title="The Alchemist by Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alchemist</a> too. Maybe this is a genre: the fantasized and personified performance art as extended motivation / self help.<br><br>I do like the carnivalesque theme and this reminded me a little of Ray Bradbury.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1556723546i/27440709._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="154" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6619538284042740239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/469365632?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ed" href="/user/show/10225206-ed">Ed</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer469365632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2298350600944354554">I had come across this book at Goodwill and opened it to the front page with all the praise from some of the leaders in business development and success. I knew I had a winner.<br/><br/>And boy did I!<br/><br/>Everything I have learned over the years from self help books, life coaches, business coaches, lectures and videos were all crammed into an ingenious novel. Trying to distill the very essence of success and inspiration through fiction is a quite a feat. What Brendan Burchard has done is nothing short of a mir</span>
  <span id="freeText2298350600944354554" style="display:none">I had come across this book at Goodwill and opened it to the front page with all the praise from some of the leaders in business development and success. I knew I had a winner.<br /><br />And boy did I!<br /><br />Everything I have learned over the years from self help books, life coaches, business coaches, lectures and videos were all crammed into an ingenious novel. Trying to distill the very essence of success and inspiration through fiction is a quite a feat. What Brendan Burchard has done is nothing short of a miracle; to have a character so thoroughly self evaluate his life through the lenses of a multitude of characters at an improbable and impossible amusement park.<br /><br />At points in the novel you can not help but to evaluate your own life. I did so at several points and realized my life so parallels that of the main character in many ways despite very different circumstances. <br /><br />I can not highly enough endorse this novel to anyone searching for purpose and success in their life.<br /><br />To say anything more would diminish both the satisfaction and revelatory nature of the book. <br /><br />Go read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2298350600944354554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer857022666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1554375658425332494">I read this book from a relative that borrowed it to me who had praised it but it fell short for my tastes. I read some of the reviews that called it contrived and hokey and I've got to admit that is exactly how I felt while reading it. The moral is good but it was a bit corny sometimes and cliche. I usually find more inspiration in books that are not necessarily meant to be "self-help" type books. It's a quick easy read though but there's nothing groundbreaking about it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27060226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27060226" />
    <a title="Jeffrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1006205-jeffrey"><img alt="Jeffrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442489375p2/1006205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27060226?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey" href="/user/show/1006205-jeffrey">Jeffrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1006205-jeffrey?shelf=self-improvement">self-improvement</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27060226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer419946674925304606">OK, first of all, let me tell you HOW I gave this book two stars. It's actually an average. I gave it 1 star for the story and 4 for intent. Since I can't give halves, it gets a 2. I'll explain story / intent below.<br/><br/>I was at a business seminar getting ideas for my business when Brendon jumped on stage and said some funny, mildly informative, and (a few) thought provoking things. Nothing spectacular here, on stage or in the book. It's really all been done and said before. But what propels people t</span>
  <span id="freeText419946674925304606" style="display:none">OK, first of all, let me tell you HOW I gave this book two stars. It's actually an average. I gave it 1 star for the story and 4 for intent. Since I can't give halves, it gets a 2. I'll explain story / intent below.<br /><br />I was at a business seminar getting ideas for my business when Brendon jumped on stage and said some funny, mildly informative, and (a few) thought provoking things. Nothing spectacular here, on stage or in the book. It's really all been done and said before. But what propels people to the top in most cases is marketing and push, push, push. There's a lot of mediocre material out there that "makes it." <br /><br />The book is rather contrived with a-man-goes-to-carnival instead of heaven theme (The Five People You Meet in Heaven) to discover truths about his life. But some serious detractors were the appearance of such characters as a wizard, a guy named Harsh the Hypnotist (Gee, what do you think he's going to be like?), and the title of chapter 3, The Truth Booth. At the end of chapter three, the main character asks, "What now?" Henry his guide replies, "Now we see the wizard." As I read this, I could hear strains of We're Off to See the Wizard rumaging about in the back of my mind. I'm sorry, but this is all too Mary-Higgins-Clark-forecasting obvious for me (Be careful, there's actually a character named Mary Higgins in the book. Really!). Brandon is obviously not a writer, so let me tell you what's going on here. <br /><br />This guy teaches how to get your stuff into the public's hands. You do so by contacting for-profit and non-profit companies. He did so. You can see by the CEO's who wrote blurbs for his book. Well, they didn't--CEO's are too busy--they probably picked from a list of blurbs. And a good point of note here is that's how it's usually done. Either people who like you or benefit from association with you (a certain percentage of the proceeds go to the companies Burchard partnered with)give you a blurb for your book. <br /><br />Also what's interesting is the people on Amazon who felt duped into having to read this book. Maybe the companies he partnered with made their employees read / buy it. Don't know. But just like email blasts on Amazon that shoots a book to number one based on who you know (joint ventures), this book will eventually fly or die on its own. With all his promoting, expert blurbs [even Jack Canfield, Mark Victor Hansen (Chicken Soup for the Soul guys), and James Redfield (The Celestine Prophecy)] it's still only doing OK on Amazon. #237,324,392 to my #365,231 (Black Body Radiation and the Ultraviolet Catastrophe), which actually got as high as 17,000 WITHOUT CORPORATE SPONSORS. Go figure. <br /><br />But he is making thousands if not millions training people to change and such, so he's used his book as an in to his profession. But in this day-n-age of the master marketer, people can shoot to the top with a book without much substance or content. So buyer beware! <br /><br />Oh, as far as intent is concerned, Brendon's heart is in the right place and he does give a percentage to charity. However, he is digging the TONS of cash piling up because of his second chance, his Golden Ticket given for another chance. So learn from Brendon how to make change as he takes your change, and then some, to the bank.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="419946674925304606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15441875075206969580">This is the first book my new book club selected. At first I thought it was going to be great, but very soon after I started reading, I found the main character deeply annoying. He just made me mad. Over and over again. The book is written too simply for me - needed a little more intrigue and wit and a better twist or something. But it has a moral point and it is a good one, if you can make it to the end. Basically I see it as yet another in a long line of the recent trend of self-help books dis</span>
  <span id="freeText15441875075206969580" style="display:none">This is the first book my new book club selected. At first I thought it was going to be great, but very soon after I started reading, I found the main character deeply annoying. He just made me mad. Over and over again. The book is written too simply for me - needed a little more intrigue and wit and a better twist or something. But it has a moral point and it is a good one, if you can make it to the end. Basically I see it as yet another in a long line of the recent trend of self-help books disguised as fictional stories. I'm tired of 'em. I don't want to focus on myself anymore. I want a real made-up story (about someone else) to read. A gripping, can't-put-it-down novel that I can't wait to run home to, crawl in bed, pull up the covers and READ for hours on end. Anybody got one of those for a change? </span>
  <a data-text-id="15441875075206969580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15927523291635703434" style="display:none">I knew nothing about Life's Golden Ticket when I downloaded it a couple weeks ago. I saw a post for the book on Facebook, read the blurb, thought it sounded interesting and downloaded it. I had not read any reviews or researched the author. I did not know what I was in for...<br /><br />Life's Golden Ticket is a book about changing lives. Imagine taking a journey into your past and witness how every decision you have made has impacted your life today. Would it be enough to make you change your actions in the future?<br /><br />“It’s a cycle of silence. You’ve lived your whole life holding in your feelings, your thoughts, your concerns, your dreams, your nightmares. You’re looping the same old story: ‘I don’t want to impose my world on anyone. . . . I don’t want to be a pest.” (Excerpt From: Burchard, Brendon. “Life's Golden Ticket.”) <br /><br />I don't catalog Life's Golden Ticket as self-help, but a profound work of fiction. I found myself evaluating my own life on multiple occasions. The struggles of our nameless main character are entirely relatable by a vast audience.<br /><br />"You see, you weren’t born feeling badly about yourself, you were taught to feel that way." (Excerpt From: Burchard, Brendon. “Life's Golden Ticket.”) </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2636038877435323739">Every once in awhile, something happens that really touches my life! Well, today I read an amazing book -- Life's Golden Ticket by Brendon Burchard! It's a fascinating story that takes place in an amusement park with little, life messages tucked away in the story! There is a special envelope that cannot be opened until the story is completed! The style was so unique -- it was a story, but it was also self-help too! What a gift reading this book has been :) </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_384506625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/384506625" />
    <a title="Diah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9583350-diah"><img alt="Diah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499607542p2/9583350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/384506625?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diah" href="/user/show/9583350-diah">Diah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789792238532" href="/book/show/5072788-life-s-golden-tiket---tiket-emas-kehidupan">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer384506625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4033439092308772826">How often do you feel happy? How often do you get stuck in a negative loop that created by yourself? Simple things like this become the main point of this book. <br/><br/>Normally I don’t read any motivation/inspiration/self-help book since I found that those kinds of book don’t have any permanent effect to “motivate or inspired or help myself” which means it IS has a effect for certain moment, like few days or weeks and I’m gonna end up thinking what I am doing is suck and won’t change anything that it’s</span>
  <span id="freeText4033439092308772826" style="display:none">How often do you feel happy? How often do you get stuck in a negative loop that created by yourself? Simple things like this become the main point of this book. <br /><br />Normally I don’t read any motivation/inspiration/self-help book since I found that those kinds of book don’t have any permanent effect to “motivate or inspired or help myself” which means it IS has a effect for certain moment, like few days or weeks and I’m gonna end up thinking what I am doing is suck and won’t change anything that it’s easier to told than actually do it. I’m pretty sarcastic and skeptical though.<br />Well, apparently more or less, this book also don’t give any permanent effect (by means I finished read this few… weeks ago?) but indeed inspired me and the moment when the very first time done reading it, I feel my heart warmed a little bit and makes me wonder that life is not, and will never be easy. <br />I mean, it is a lovely story. And the synopsis in the back cover has nothing to do with the story (yeah I’m going to give a bit spoiler….)<br />So, this man (I don’t know his name, is it Brendon?) is normal, common man that live in America, confusing with career and relationship mainly about his life and he has a fight with his current fiancée and just blow things up and right after the fight, his fiancée (Mary) just got in a car accident near an abandoned amusement park and can’t help clinging in a bed and machine and dying in the hospital. She gave him a mysterious envelope and told him to go there (the park) to know what actually happened to her and, and yeah sadly then she died.<br />The man visited the abandoned and deserted amusement park and well it suddenly, magically turns out into a life and every single rides is working and there are a lot of people there (I know how stupid and childish it sounds but…) then he met an old, wise and friendly ground housekeeper and also other park employees (circus dudes, and gypsy fortune-teller you know, kind of people you meet at the amusement carnival park) and in every time he try the rides like roller coaster and other carousel it just teach him more about his life and people around him, especially Mary what follows an unforgettable journey of personal transformation and finally uncover what happens to Mary and discover what’s inside the mysterious envelope and find out the people who gives her that. And the ending, it is happy ending I guess. Happy and touching ending indeed (;_____;) *sob*<br />I was cried because I felt exactly feeling like the way the main character feeling about his life, his lost, redemption, and finally, let go. And I just love the way Brendon mix things up between reality and fantasy. Frankly speaking, it was the first time I read sort-of-self-help-book that written in such a touching fictional and a lovely story. I mean, I’m glued to it like literally can’t stop reading. <br />P.S : I just hate it the background story about Brendon got car accident, I hate professional motivator (even Brendon Burchard is actually good looking) and the drama about him almost die in car accident in developing country is overexposed and overrated  I mean yeah if he weren’t crashed his car this book will never be existed but the content and the story and the message behind the story is most valuable thing compared to anything. <br /><br />The book presents a fictional fantasy and philosophy that is lightweight and gives a little insight for those who want to make sense of life is soo simple: the courage to forgive yourself and confront the past to achieve a desired life. Highly recommended :)And I don’t know if self-help book and inspirational book are the same.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4033439092308772826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167820378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167820378" />
    <a title="Angee Bartlett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4833650-angee-bartlett"><img alt="Angee Bartlett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300132272p2/4833650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167820378?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angee Bartlett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angee Bartlett" href="/user/show/4833650-angee-bartlett">Angee Bartlett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167820378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17953271783895623448">When my friend suggested I read this, I was a bit skeptical. She assured me it was a quick read and that I would learn a lot from it.<br/><br/>Okay, I gave it a try and was more than pleasantly surprised. Brendan Burchard has written a truly great book. I laughed, I cried, and I thought. It brought memories to the surface that had been long buried and made me think about where I am going with my life.<br/><br/>The main character narrates his fantasy trip which takes place in an abandoned amusement park that isn't a</span>
  <span id="freeText17953271783895623448" style="display:none">When my friend suggested I read this, I was a bit skeptical. She assured me it was a quick read and that I would learn a lot from it.<br /><br />Okay, I gave it a try and was more than pleasantly surprised. Brendan Burchard has written a truly great book. I laughed, I cried, and I thought. It brought memories to the surface that had been long buried and made me think about where I am going with my life.<br /><br />The main character narrates his fantasy trip which takes place in an abandoned amusement park that isn't abandoned when he arrives. The people in the park give invited visitors a second chance at changing their lives for the better, hence the golden ticket.<br /><br />He is at the park at the request of his dying fiance who had been missing for 40 days. Each person he meets at the park and each carnival ride he takes shows him his past both good and bad. Each lesson he learns will help him - risk changing his life, forgive both himself and others, be bold, see the other person's side of an argument, learn how to contribute and a host of life skills one needs to be successful.<br /><br />This is a very good self-help book that is easy to read, easy to understand, and inspirational for people who would like to change but hate self-help books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17953271783895623448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1160301227507068297">I was expecting a life-changing book wrapped into a nice story.<br/>But I found « self-help » cliché along a flat story line.<br/><br/>Some of those themes are:<br/>- Take responsibility<br/>- Set goals<br/>- Ask yourself Who do you want to become<br/>- Question your beliefs<br/>- The power of visualization<br/>- Fight your fears<br/>- Don't give up…<br/><br/>It could be a good reminder, but I would say:<br/>- Either get a solid Self-help book. You’ll grasp all those concepts in a better way, with more catchy/accurate sentences.<br/>- Or get a book with a really n</span>
  <span id="freeText1160301227507068297" style="display:none">I was expecting a life-changing book wrapped into a nice story.<br />But I found « self-help » cliché along a flat story line.<br /><br />Some of those themes are:<br />- Take responsibility<br />- Set goals<br />- Ask yourself Who do you want to become<br />- Question your beliefs<br />- The power of visualization<br />- Fight your fears<br />- Don't give up…<br /><br />It could be a good reminder, but I would say:<br />- Either get a solid Self-help book. You’ll grasp all those concepts in a better way, with more catchy/accurate sentences.<br />- Or get a book with a really nice story that will touch your heart, and that you can dream about afterwards.<br /><br />The one thing i liked is this idea we all want to change our "just ok life", but 90% of us won't. We all get caught up in our daily routines. We all prefer security over risks. We all end up accepting a "limited" life. Change won't happen just realizing it, and saying "I want to change".<br /><br />I usually take notes along my reading. I didn’t find anything new or worthwhile here.<br /><br />I got disappointed with this one, but still, I want to try others from the same author: "The Millionaire Messenger", "High Performance Habits", "The Motivation Manifesto".</span>

And it is useless. </span>

<div id="review_3049842871" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3049842871" />
    <a title="ReadingMama" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4842743-readingmama"><img alt="ReadingMama" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295539811p2/4842743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3049842871?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ReadingMama" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ReadingMama" href="/user/show/4842743-readingmama">ReadingMama</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3049842871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12378086135013238812">While I was waiting for “The Millionaire messenger”, this inspirational novel popped up by the same author. This book reminds me of “The five people you meet in heaven” by Mitch Albom, and “The Alchemist” by Paolo Coehlo; It is a quest of personal transformation. Henry goes to an old amusement park where he encounters so many experiences forcing him to revising his past, some beautiful, others painful, yet all of them teaching him life lesson.. In the truth booth, he learns how his abusive child</span>
  <span id="freeText12378086135013238812" style="display:none">While I was waiting for “The Millionaire messenger”, this inspirational novel popped up by the same author. This book reminds me of “The five people you meet in heaven” by Mitch Albom, and “The Alchemist” by Paolo Coehlo; It is a quest of personal transformation. Henry goes to an old amusement park where he encounters so many experiences forcing him to revising his past, some beautiful, others painful, yet all of them teaching him life lesson.. In the truth booth, he learns how his abusive childhood made him feeling inadequate, ugly, weak and useless… The world is a dark and dangerous place. As he visits the following places, Screaming Carnies, Harsh the Hypnotist, Gus and the Elephant, Hall of Mirrors, and finally Tunnel of Love, he is becoming more empathetic, confident and willing to restore the relationship with himself and others. In the end, this is a story of love, loss and redemption. We are all given a life’s golden ticket to live our life to its fullest… how are we going to use it?<br />“Did I live?” “Did I live it fully the way God has designed?” “Did I love?” “Did I love openly, fully and completely?” After the author, Brendon survived a horrific car accident, he dedicates his life for inspiring others fulfilling their dreams and finding their destinies. This little book helps me to reflect my own life and reminds me how I should live. In the life’s journeys up and down; good and bad, I must take the responsibility. Be bold and contribute to the world. Forgive other’s mistakes because they all have their own cross to bear and unique life experiences that made them who they are. We all have a life’s golden ticket. Every morning I need to realize that this is my second chance. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12378086135013238812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lynn Coullard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97180002-lynn-coullard"><img alt="Lynn Coullard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585397692p2/97180002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3169260086?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_2698756789" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2698756789" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2698756789?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kolya Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kolya Smith" href="/user/show/93005416-kolya-smith">Kolya Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93005416-kolya-smith?shelf=never-read">never-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2698756789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4262475484117607823"><br/>Last night, I had a terrible, unpleasant experience with productivity guru, Brendon Burchard.<br/>On January 29th, he sent out an email saying - You all loved transformation week so much that we’ve decided to share my ENTIRE Wellness Master Class with you at NO COST over the next 10 days. I’m sharing the ENTIRE course via my podcast as well as via video on this page. But fair warning: Each episode is only up for 72 hours, so enjoy it now.<br/>Fast forward to yesterday, no new email sent out about Day 3, i</span>
  <span id="freeText4262475484117607823" style="display:none"><br />Last night, I had a terrible, unpleasant experience with productivity guru, Brendon Burchard.<br />On January 29th, he sent out an email saying - You all loved transformation week so much that we’ve decided to share my ENTIRE Wellness Master Class with you at NO COST over the next 10 days. I’m sharing the ENTIRE course via my podcast as well as via video on this page. But fair warning: Each episode is only up for 72 hours, so enjoy it now.<br />Fast forward to yesterday, no new email sent out about Day 3, it was still locked, no Day 3 on the podcast! As I researched further into it, I found out that he shared a broken link to the class (because you had to sign up within 48 hours - if you miss out on the window of time, you have to pay $99 for the class) and he wanted to make sure that people missed that window of opportunity. One person said that it worked if they clicked “Back To Home” and when someone complained, he shared a 2nd link and there was a third, link, when people still didn’t have access to Day 3. People thought they signed up, but it didn’t take. I called them out on it and last night, the link was fixed within 15 minutes, and the podcasts and videos are up this morning, after I told them I was contacting the attorney general. Last night I took a photo at 8:23 and only Day 1 and 2 were up for the podcasts. And 9:42 they deleted Day 1 podcast. I got an email in between those times at 8:29, referring me to another website. They completely blew me off. At 9:38 I told them I was contacting the attorney general, which is why by 9:42 they had deleted Day 1 and fixed the broken link. They could have gotten away with passing the buck to the other website, but that didn’t explain the podcasts not being up, as promised. Then later they hid one of my comments and then when I called them out on it they unhid it. And then after a while I was unable to tag the people I was communicating with, exposing his scheme.<br />These slimy business practices are all too common with people like this. And the most tragic thing to me is that they can say great things, but once they do something slimy, it loses its power.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4262475484117607823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1856200846" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1856200846" />
    <a title="Kristina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51747966-kristina"><img alt="Kristina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467822854p2/51747966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1856200846?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristina" href="/user/show/51747966-kristina">Kristina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1856200846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11967531173966308470">One of the most trite books I’ve ever read. If you like reading explicit and simplified explanations of what you should learn through years of therapy, this book is for you. The author may want to consider an accompanying workbook so readers can easily work out their life’s problems like the main character. To give the author a head start, I offer this:<br/><br/>“Write down the five worst memories from your childhood. What themes do you see? How did this change how you viewed life and the world? How has t</span>
  <span id="freeText11967531173966308470" style="display:none">One of the most trite books I’ve ever read. If you like reading explicit and simplified explanations of what you should learn through years of therapy, this book is for you. The author may want to consider an accompanying workbook so readers can easily work out their life’s problems like the main character. To give the author a head start, I offer this:<br /><br />“Write down the five worst memories from your childhood. What themes do you see? How did this change how you viewed life and the world? How has this impacted you as an adult?”<br /><br />“Do you have an open or closed mindset?”<br /><br />“What would you say to the person who hurt you most if they were siting right in front of you?”<br /><br />If you like circus themed life cliches then this is the book for you. <br /><br />Go ahead and read the golden tickets at the back of the book if you already own it. It neither adds nor detracts from the story. <br /><br />Here is my favorite part:<br /> “My hands felt numb, as if I had dipped them in snow and then entered a warm room.”<br /><br />I wish my friend could get her $4 back from Barnes &amp; Nobles. We don’t know what to do with it now that we both read it. Maybe donate it to the library so no one else has to waste $4 to find out what a crappy book it is.<br /><br />If you really need self-help books, read Brene Brown.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11967531173966308470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4992152-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434486014p2/4992152.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/4992152-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone feeling a little low</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4992152-susan?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4992152-susan?shelf=recommends-to-others">recommends-to-others</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4992152-susan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159806458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15288801430489067092">I thought this book was amazing. Some of it was a little like ok so everyone is explaining their life story, but ultimately it made you look at yourself. it was simple to grasp the concepts in the story and exciting to read. you wanted to read the story because well, theme parks are cool. <br/><br/>It was lovely, not in a way where you would cry or anything like that. But just on the realisation that you know things can be different. I read it thinking about people I know living lives they find unfulfilli</span>
  <span id="freeText15288801430489067092" style="display:none">I thought this book was amazing. Some of it was a little like ok so everyone is explaining their life story, but ultimately it made you look at yourself. it was simple to grasp the concepts in the story and exciting to read. you wanted to read the story because well, theme parks are cool. <br /><br />It was lovely, not in a way where you would cry or anything like that. But just on the realisation that you know things can be different. I read it thinking about people I know living lives they find unfulfilling and I thought, you know I've always refused to lead my life that way, however in the last few years I can see how people get caught up in that "rut". They needn't. I needn't.<br /><br />Anyways, I think everyone, especially my husband and closest family should read the book. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EA/A1rTLmKPKT6edk/bQDn5JhlcjvEdsc21CzU+PZ7z36vxnGIyB93Q68WmBkpr6vzrRrpNTq9Q29oEtfn7ExA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mC9PqOz+NAr48J8y8oWrRkDe1ujV+2kGwJDMZeYX8pB/ynMZQLktXkaFycbg4eGyga2BEWUUhb6FCw+F1+ZR6A==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2829441517621917196">BRENDON BURCHARD is the author of the New York Times bestselling book, THE CHARGE, and the #1 New York Times bestseller THE MILLIONAIRE MESSENGER. He is also founder of High Performance Academy, the legendary personal development program for achievers, and Experts Academy, the world's most comprehensive marketing training program for aspiring authors, speakers, coaches, and online thought leaders.</span>
  <span id="freeText2829441517621917196" style="display:none">BRENDON BURCHARD is the author of the New York Times bestselling book, THE CHARGE, and the #1 New York Times bestseller THE MILLIONAIRE MESSENGER. He is also founder of High Performance Academy, the legendary personal development program for achievers, and Experts Academy, the world's most comprehensive marketing training program for aspiring authors, speakers, coaches, and online thought leaders. For these works, Brendon is recognized as one of the top trainers in the world on the topics of both motivation and marketing.<br /><br />Brendon's books, videos, newsletters, products, and appearances now inspire two million people a month worldwide. <br /><br />Brendon was blessed to receive life's golden ticket -- a second chance -- after surviving a car accident in a developing country. Since then, he has dedicated his life to helping individuals, teams, and organizations find their charge, share their voice, and make a greater difference in the world.<br /><br />Brendon is regularly seen on public television, and he has been in media appearances on Anderson Cooper, ABC World News, Wall Street Journal TV, NPR stations, Oprah and Friends, and other popular outlets like SUCCESS magazine, Inc.com, Forbes.com, FastCompany.com, and the Huffington Post.<br /><br />As one of the most in-demand trainers of our time, Brendon has shared the stage with the Dalai Lama, Sir Richard Branson, Tony Hsieh, Tony Robbins, Wayne Dyer, Stephen Covey, Deepak Chopra, David Bach, John Gray, Jack Canfield, Tim Ferriss, and more. His clients include entrepreneurs and executives from 59 countries, and his advice and training has been in use at, or sought by, Accenture, Alcoa, Amazon.com, The United States Naval Academy, and 34 or the top 50 universities in the world.<br /><br />Brendon's recent online marketing campaigns have set records in publishing, online product launches, and live video broadcast revenue, and he has become the go-to marketing advisor for many of the most successful companies and celebrities in the world. Anderson Cooper calls Brendon "one of the top marketing and business trainers in the world." <br /><br />Brendon blogs on his FB page at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/brendonburchardfan">http://www.facebook.com/brendonburcha...</a></span>
